<Text>I was visiting SF for a week and gave myself the weekend to play in the bathroom area. I found Golden Gate Rides and met Daniel how was very helpful and generous in renting me a bike.

I got my hands on a hard tail giant in excellent shape, hardly ridden. I tuned up the brakes a bit first but the drive train was in excellent shape, smooth shifting. Daniel hooked me up with a helmet, a lot and a tool bag with flat repair kit (tube, patches, CO2  tire irons and multi-tool). I paid $28 for a half day and got the next full day half off for $20.

For a higher price they have top notch road and mtn bikes for good shredding in the area and they'll shuttle you to your destination for a small charge - neat service I may use next time to explore farther away.

I took the bike around the city - golden gate park out to the ocean beach and lands end the first day. On the second I went over the golden gate and up and around the Marin Headlands, rodeo beach and Golden Gate recreation Area. The bike was solid the whole way. I noticed bikes from other companies were heavily branded (ex BLAZING SADDLES! COME RENT ME) makes people instantly identifiable as tourists and the bikes don't look as nice.

The location is in the tenderloin, which some consider seedy, but I had no problem or fears visiting their store front or returning after dark. It's not as bad as people say (nice speakeasy across the street).

Highly recommend! A bike can take you wonderful places.</Text>< Pictures>

<review>8 dollars an hour to rent bikes.  I live in this building.  See the owner Bigyan every day.  Super nice guy.  What's cool about this for locals is it's not right inside Union Square with the rest of those bike shops where nobody knows where they should be going.

TOURISTS, what's good about this place just a short walk from your Union Square hotel is that you're NOT renting bikes right next to a parking garage.  Car rental companies lease space from them, then rent cars to TOURISTS, who also have no clue where they're going and then end up hitting you.

Golden Gate Rides is just a short 5 minute walk and besides, after all you're going on a "bike ride" ;)

Use your time wisely as a warm up, then stretch outside while your bike is readying.

Cheers and enjoy SF< /review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPNkRyAY33RUWjD8S_ba1_fJVN_f2EfY0f8aTef=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNOn9vQF12uh30ckjUcztX1SCOxzTaP__zubFc6=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]<//Pics><gmap_id>0x8085809026bcafeb:0x556925488b497e01< /gmap_id>< Date>

Woke up at 0500 and picked up my bike at 0645. The rental shop owner is really really nice and supportive.
Knowing I am going for a long ride (actually not really long, from SF to Mountain View), he gave me everything I may need in case of emergency, including the compressed-air tank, spare tube, as well as phone mount, which I worried about before picking the bike, as I didn't have a phone mount (for sure it's important for riding to somewhere new to me).
Regarding the bike, the quality is awesome, and I didn't get flat tire about 100km ride.
I have been to other bike shops before, but this one is definitely the only option I would consider if I have to pick one.<//text>

<time>1469449077692< /time>< Text>
We had an amazing experience with this company. There is a price reduction if you rent the bikes more than one day, the bikes were high quality bikes (light and good gears) which were excellent maintained. Also we got a lot of personal advise for which streets we should use or avoid. Which is very handy in a city with the hills of San Francisco. Also they had a fun picture game going on which gave our bike ride a playful touch. They offer a free service to come and repair your tire when it's flat, a service we luckily did not have to use.
When I look to the quality of the other bikes which are rented in the city and combine it with the personal service, I can only conclude this is the best bike rental service in San Francisco.< /Text>

1531185008298</Time>
<Rating>1</Rating>< text>
Rented four electric bikes for a sunny day in SF and were told the range on the bikes would be 20-30 miles, depending on how efficient you ride it. Went through the planned route with one of the employees and some quick instructions and we were on our way.

Just after a few miles we noticed the battery level on two of the bikes were already starting to decrease fast, so we tried to ride them as efficient as possible, but after reaching 12-13 miles two of the bikes were already the lowest battery level so we were expecting them to die pretty soon.

At this point we were in Sausalito so we had to ditch our planned route of coming back over the brigde and decided to take the ferry instead, due to the low battery level. This ended up costing us an extra 12.5$ pr. person. After getting off the ferry we drove through the city and ended up getting back to the shop with the battery still holding up on all bikes, which was an positive suprise.

Upon arrival one on the employees asked us if everything was as expected and told them about the battery indicator being at the lowest point very early and about two of the backbrakes not being 100% on the bikes. Did not get the chance to mention this at the site, but the suspension on all bike were really poor also, which made the ride uncomfortable.

This eventually led up to me having a longer discussion with the manager that totally ruined this experience us. Whatever we told him, there would follow a longer explanation as to why we were wrong and he was right, not willing to listen to what we had to say. Instead, he kept on talking about unrelated matters and trying to steer away from the real issue, that the bikes performed poorly. Eventually we got him to take one of the bikes out and got him to admit that the brakes were not working 100%. From the discussion we learned that we had also not been given all of the instructions needed as to how the bike and battery indicator works, and the manager at this point told us that we should read the manual before riding a bike like this (what?).

The experience in itself was maybe three stars, but followed by an discussion with an arrogant manager, not willing to listen to what his customer has to say, I see no option to give this just the one star. Expensive as well, several cheaper companies in the area.</text>

<Rate>5</Rate><Review>I am REALLY impressed by this place. I went after a friend mentioned that Les Claypool (of Primus) had a winery in Sonoma County.

The wines are not inexpensive, but they are worth the price. I was not charged for tasting, as I bought a couple bottles, and the pours are generous. Surprisingly, they even had their champagne (from France, so it is OK to call it champagne) open for tasting. Their prices for tasting are pretty normal, starting around $20.

The tasting room is intimate; there is seating for 10 or so. There is a good selection of shirts, glasses, etc. for sale as well. The lady pouring casually mentioned that Les will not be in as he's on tour, but implied that he is often in the tasting room.

Thank you Claypool Cellars for a great experience, I will definitely visit again soon!

Update June 2019:

@jamsjoybungalow food truck present serving awesome south Asian cuisine. I had the pleasure of meeting Les Claypool, and was treated to a wonderful glass of 2018 Ros√© and a generous pour of the 2014 Sonoma Coast Pinot Noir.

Once again the service was AMAZING, and Les was totally awesome even though I was a bit akward. Thanks for a great time! See you soon!< /Review><Pictures>None< /Pictures><userid>108472585116402272784< /userid></record>

112219625742959183656< /userid>
<Date>1503191331872< /Date>< Review>
I love Lam's. I have lunch here at least twice a week. The food is delicious, fresh, and inexpensive. It's a family-run business and they make a point of knowing their good customers' names and their preferences. The kitchen is squeaky clean. The decor makes it a place that you're not going to seek out for date night, but if you want tasty, no-frills Chinese food you won't be disappointed. Weekday lunch is their busy time when it seems like every construction trade worker in Marin descends at the same time. Favorites include the wah wonton soup,  green bean prawns, mu shu  anything, and spicy eggplant chicken.</Review>

< Text>
The customer service and willingness to help was well above expectation.
However, I don't trust their mechanic's suggestions or his / her analysis.
Early this year (March 2020) I experienced a problem with my car and noticed water and oil are mixed in the radiator.

I took the car to my Mechanic and dealer ship and both claim the problem is head gas gate.The dealership took the car and worked with Hyundai (due to some prior re-calls) and supposedly fix the problem (Hyundai factory request for an additional analysis and confirmed the problem is not head gas gate and it is something else),

I left the car with the dealership to repair. After few days they claimed the car is fixed and return the car. The repair cost partially paid by Hyundai (due to prior re-calls) and I was charged for $350 and I was told they checked everything and the car is totally fixed.

After 3 months and about 150 miles (due to Covid-19 I work from home and don't drive that much) I checked the radiator and engine oil and both were totally empty (There were no antifreeze or oil drop in my dive way where the car was parked).

I return the car back to dealership after a day they call me back to tell me  the antifreeze is licking from the upper radiator  hose and suggested to change the upper and the lower hose for the price of about $650.

I did not trust their finding since few months earlier (March 2020), I replaced the radiator hose and I knew that can't be the reason.

Therefore, I took the car to my own mechanic and he checked the radiator with the pressure cap and determined the problem is the lick from the radiator itself and indicate this problem is related to the previous issue and should have been fixed before.

Summary,
Stevens Creek Hyundai refuse to check or accept the problem is the radiator itself and not the hose.
I believe this dealership will fix your car if is under Manufacture re-calls but also they propose unnecessary repairs and make the customer to pay for services that they may not need.</Text>

I recently purchased a used 2016 Hyundai Genesis Coupe, and unfortunately I had an issue with the trunk latch. As the car was still under warranty I decided to have it fixed at a dealership before my mother was coming into town on the 21st. The gentleman helping me out was the assistant service manager Eric Yaeger. As I dropped off the car he was incredibly curt with no tact, telling me I spoke too quickly and unclear. I was incredibly put off by his behavior, which was rude for someone that was dealing directly with customers. He told me it would be done at the end of the day.

The service center closed at 6pm, and I hadn't received a phone call by 5pm, so I called them. They didn't answer and I was worried as I hadn't prepared a mode of transportation if they hadn't finished my vehicle. He finally called me to tell me that the part wasn't available and I could come get my vehicle. On the way there he called back to tell me they couldn't close my trunk so I had to get a rental. I was then taken to a nearby Enterprise where they did not have any comparable Hyundai cars available. Eric had assured me they would take care of it and when I called him he said to have "Samantha do the usual". Enterprise informed me that she had been fired due to this practice of loaning out cars that weren't Hyundai and writing them off as Hyundai. Sketchy, as heck.

I went back to pick up my house keys which I had forgotten there on Friday and noticed that my windshield had 2 deep cracks in it that were not there before. When they had taken my car they had marked all the spots with issues, and it had not been marked. One of them was so deep it went through to the inside of the car. There also was a lot of trash that had been put into my trunk. I was not pleased they were using it as a refuse bin. I informed Eric who told me that they were not responsible for anything that happened to my car. I was incredibly irritated and now worried for the rest of my car as it was sitting out in the middle of their lot.

Eric told me my car would be ready on Monday, which unfortunately was midway into my mom's vacation, but I tried to keep positive. Around 5pm on Monday I hadn't received a call so again I had to call Eric. He told me that he had JUST received the part right then and it wouldn't be done today. I asked him if he was going to call me when it was done on Tuesday, and he said "Of course, how would you know to come pick it up?". Well, he hadn't called me the last 2 times so I had very little confidence he remembered any of his customers at all. Incredibly upset with his unprofessional behavior as I work in the service industry as a manager and I do not tolerate that behavior from myself or employees -- it is not how you get repeat customers or a good reputation.

I had also asked Eric while they had my vehicle to check if the seal needed repair on the drivers side door as I heard a whooshing noise when I drove above 40mph. When I inquired on Friday if it had been fixed Eric told me to my face that they had driven it and heard no noise whatsoever. I absolutely hate being lied to and I was incredibly disappointed, as I still have the whooshing noise.

I did pick up my car today, and as it was sitting out in the dusty lot the entire 6 days, it was dirty as heck. So far the trunk does work, a silver lining. Long story short, I have seen a lot of reviews touting other Hyundai dealerships over this one. I had not checked reviews prior to taking my car here, but I wish I had. Not only was my car damaged but the assistant service manager lied to my face about checking out an issue I had asked for, and in general was rude as hell. Take your car here if you don't mind 0 communication, poor service, and collateral damage. Now I'm going to go clean out the trash in my trunk and pay $200 to fix the cracks in my windshield. Thanks Hyundai Stevens Creek. Never again.<//Review>
